  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1c45e10f-3142-4e5d-ab2d-cf34e62dd558'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer13811549488083606098"><b><i><br/>9/9/16...After watching the NFL opener last night - GO BRONCOS! - I feel like setting everything else aside and re-reading one of my all-time favorite football series again...<br/><br/>10/19/15...Re-read...<br/><br/>I've read this so many times, if it were a paperback, the pages would be worn out. Just LOVE it.</i> <br/><br/>Every time.<br/><br/>5+++++ Sweet Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445368364ra/16638646.gif' width='500' height='235' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book was like a mix of <i>Legally Blonde, A Cinderella Story</i> (that movie with Hilary Duff), <i>Beautiful Disaster</i>, completely over the top family drama and possessiveness, spikes </span>
  <span id="freeText13811549488083606098" style="display:none"><b><i><br>9/9/16...After watching the NFL opener last night - GO BRONCOS! - I feel like setting everything else aside and re-reading one of my all-time favorite football series again...<br><br>10/19/15...Re-read...<br><br>I've read this so many times, if it were a paperback, the pages would be worn out. Just LOVE it.</i> <br><br>Every time.<br><br>5+++++ Sweet Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445368364ra/16638646.gif" width="500" height="235" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book was like a mix of <i>Legally Blonde, A Cinderella Story</i> (that movie with Hilary Duff), <i>Beautiful Disaster</i>, completely over the top family drama and possessiveness, spikes of Alabama football, and the ridiculous names of Molly <i>Juliet Shakespeare</i> and <i>Romeo Prince</i>...all with with an English flair to sweeten the kitty...and I inhaled it like a Dyson. <br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445368316i/16638641._SX540_.jpg" width="368" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am a total sucker for the hot guy falls for the nerd stories. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445368316i/16638642._SX540_.jpg" width="368" height="207" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's shameful. It's cliche. And I'm not sorry. <br><br>And if you take that theme AND add sports, and alpha male, AND random Shakespearean and Monty Python references?!?! <br><br><b>Holeeeeeeee. Shite.</b><br><br>Mind BLOWN. <br><br>I enjoyed the fuck out of this story. <br><br>Molly was really sweet and level-headed and I liked her a lot. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445368316i/16638643.jpg" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And Romeo was swoon-worthy. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445368316i/16638644.jpg" width="316" height="421" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I just LOVED them. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445368316ra/16638645.gif" width="500" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>There was also a decent supporting cast and an engaging plot, which I always love. I'm looking forward to reading more from this author. </span>

<div id="review_743956587" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/743956587" />
    <a title="• Lisa •" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11963959-lisa"><img alt="• Lisa •" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576172089p2/11963959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/743956587?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="• Lisa •" class="user" itemprop="url" name="• Lisa •" href="/user/show/11963959-lisa">• Lisa •</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to • Lisa • by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/6852653-patrycja">Patrycja</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11963959-lisa?shelf=addicted-to-this-author">addicted-to-this-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer743956587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3574395125667028260"><b>5 ROME AND MOL STARS.</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"So are you to my thoughts as food to life, or as sweet seasoned showers are to the ground." - William Shakespeare.</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382309477i/5807256._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='500' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Calling all lovers of the slightly angsty NA genre with a gorgeous hero with anger issues, and a feisty geek chic heroine. I will not make any apologies for my (slightly predictable by now) Lisa style gushing review, I felt so at home with this book I've decided that if me and this author ever meet we would be firm friends. What a sweet, sexy, dramatic and p</span>
  <span id="freeText3574395125667028260" style="display:none"><b>5 ROME AND MOL STARS.</b><br><br><b>
  <i>"So are you to my thoughts as food to life, or as sweet seasoned showers are to the ground." - William Shakespeare.</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382309477i/5807256._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Calling all lovers of the slightly angsty NA genre with a gorgeous hero with anger issues, and a feisty geek chic heroine. I will not make any apologies for my (slightly predictable by now) Lisa style gushing review, I felt so at home with this book I've decided that if me and this author ever meet we would be firm friends. What a sweet, sexy, dramatic and perfectly romantic story of college star crossed lovers. Warning proceed with caution, I loved this book so I may just be a tad dramatically over the top with my book love, here are my 'sweet home' book thoughts ...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382298303i/5796438._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>What's it all about?</b><br>English born and all round studious, croc wearing geek Molly Shakespeare has the opportunity to study and lecture abroad in an all American college so when this lonely twenty year old hits the university of Alabama she expects to stick to her studies and live her life how she knows best - on her own. Romeo Prince is the university star quarter back his specialities include his bullet arm and charming the ladies into his bed. Both these characters have a troubled past, both these characters feel the depth of loneliness neither of them expected to find eachother. 'Sweet home' is the story of Rome and Mol a duo who couldn't be more different, a tale of opposites attract and finding true love. But will they be able to hold on to each other when everything stands against them? This NA story shows how love can change everything, all in one summer in Alabama.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382309855i/5807490._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>What did I love?</b><br>Let me start by saying that I love a stateside college romance, everything about a book that showcases the lifestyle of American colleges has me hooked, so couple that with a fantastically British feel and you know that this book was ticking some serious five star boxes for me. This book had British references galore, but for me she was authentic on both counts, the author told her story with confidence; the writing was fluid and engaging and utterly full of romance. The whole story was filled with gorgeous, swoon worthy moments of heart-in-mouth loveliness. The first kiss was knee-knocking, heart melting standard and I'm sure if I'm having a bad day re reading that scene over and over again wont be totally out of the question. I really enjoyed the books cute spin off references to Romeo and Juliet and I love nothing more than a beauty and the beast/make over type scenario played out in my books and this gorgeous number hosts all that and more. Onto the characters, even though there was a 'seen this before' familiarity with the character types I didn't mind, I really fell for both the leading and secondary characters. Molly Shakespeare was geeky, outspoken, wonderfully English and totally unaware of her 'fall in love' with quality charms, I never once found her background and hardships annoying she was in my opinion completely adorable. Romeo Prince was heavenly; he was sweet, alpha, tormented and gorgeous in one American style football star package and I was sold. Molly and Romeo are heart warmingly sweet and sincere, she is his lucky charm, he is her family, there was not a moment where I didnt doubt or fall more in love with their connection. The whole package worked for me, this author really made the story work for my reading tastes and I'm excited to see more books released by this talented writer.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382309477i/5807259._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Final thoughts ...</b><br>Undoubtably there will be 'those' readers that find holes in this story, they will talk about a predictability factor and they will most likely compare it to similar books in the genre but for me I ignored all those things because the enjoyment factor was top notch. I can't express how much I enjoyed this story, I had gigantic case of the book butterflies and and I could not put this addictive page turner down. This story will not be for all, it has some over the top drama, one controlling hero and some bad decisions made along the way, but it also has some laugh out loud moments, some hotter than hot bed time action, two unforgettable characters and a group of best friends that you'll fall in love with, so If like me you enjoy this genre then don't delay, go grab it readers. Enjoy ... Kisses.<br><br><br><b>
  <i>❤Bezzie buddy read with my gorgeous Anna.❤</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3574395125667028260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_756045843" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/756045843" />
    <a title="A" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4541235-a"><img alt="A" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/756045843?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="A" class="user" itemprop="url" name="A" href="/user/show/4541235-a">A</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4541235-a?shelf=festivals-of-stupidity">festivals-of-stupidity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4541235-a?shelf=don-t-need-no-stinking-research">don-t-need-no-stinking-research</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4541235-a?shelf=don-t-need-no-stinking-editing">don-t-need-no-stinking-editing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4541235-a?shelf=fake-yanks">fake-yanks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4541235-a?shelf=versimilitude-is-a-four-letter-word">versimilitude-is-a-four-letter-word</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer756045843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13231964388950127668">Dear authors,<br/><br/>If you are British, and you must set a book in a specific American location, then, for the love of anything that you hold dear, DO SOME BLOODY (for the Brits) FUCKING (for everyone) RESEARCH.<br/><br/>Let us count the ways in which this book is just WRONG.<br/><br/>1) Our "heroine," Molly Juliet Shakespeare (I know, I know) is a 20 year old graduate student at the University of Alabama. <br/><br/>Yet somehow, Molly is housed by the university with undergraduate students. <br/><br/>Yeah, but NO. Graduate students have thei</span>
  <span id="freeText13231964388950127668" style="display:none">Dear authors,<br /><br />If you are British, and you must set a book in a specific American location, then, for the love of anything that you hold dear, DO SOME BLOODY (for the Brits) FUCKING (for everyone) RESEARCH.<br /><br />Let us count the ways in which this book is just WRONG.<br /><br />1) Our "heroine," Molly Juliet Shakespeare (I know, I know) is a 20 year old graduate student at the University of Alabama. <br /><br />Yet somehow, Molly is housed by the university with undergraduate students. <br /><br />Yeah, but NO. Graduate students have their own housing.<br /><br />2) Molly is the TA, but is introduced as a fellow student by the professor. <br /><br />Yeah, but NO. She is not taking the class as a student. <br /><br />3) Molly is instantly challenged by your typical nasty mean girl bitch who basically tells Molly - someone the bitch just met - that Molly is a pathetic loser. In front of the entire class. <br /><br />Yeah, but NO. Even mean girl undergraduate bitches understand that graduate TAs DO ALL THE GRADING. So mean girl bitch - in the real world - would have just gotten herself a big fat failing grade. Or at the least, a warning and a referral to the student conduct council. Most schools - and I have to believe 'Bama would be the same - have a code of conduct for students and the mean girl stepped over it. <br /><br />4) Molly's undergraduate roommates take Molly to pledge a sorority.<br /><br />OK. Words fail me to describe just how RIDICULOUS this scene was. No sorority rush works this way. The pinning takes place first (?!?!) and THEN the rounds of parties?!? And the final party is not some sort of a preference night, but a toga party?!??!! (Because Animal House is SO 2013.) And Molly's SENIOR YEAR roommates are finally getting into a top sorority despite failing to make the cut three years in a row?!?!?!<br /><br />No. No. NOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOO.<br /><br />5) Molly's Goth, senior year roommate wants to be in a sorority because she thinks this will make her a cheerleader. At 'Bama. At the start of the fall semester<br /><br />Let's look at this set up again. A SENIOR wants to be a cheerleader. Even though football season should already be in progress by this date, and the cheerleaders would have been selected long before. Also, we're talking 'BAMA. Where football is a religion, and cheerleaders aren't far behind.<br /><br />6) The pledges are initiated by kissing a boy and guessing what he just ate. <br /><br />I'm going to let the horror of this sink in. As if this wouldn't get the sorority kicked off campus before one could utter "Roll Tide." Also, sorority initiation? Is more than just a kiss and keg (and like a keg would be involved in the first place!)<br /><br />7) I'm stopping before I get to the football. Because from what I've heard, Tilly's depiction is more rage inducing than her sorority mishegas.<br /><br />Look, I get it, this is supposed to be some big swoony if paint by numbers New Adult romance. (Although the characters are more caricatures than three-dimensional humans. The prologue flashback to Molly's childhood is saccharine and on-the-nose, and was wholly unnecessary. Molly is your usual "woe is me, I'm so ordinary and nerdy" NA heroine, while the hero, Romeo (I KNOW, I KNOW) is defined by his abs more than anything resembling actual personality. Everyone says "darlin'" and "ain't" all the time and drop the "g''s off the end of their sentences so the reader knows we are in the SOUTH, doncha know. I'm surprised Scarlett and Rhett don't show up just to rub that in more. And the Americans are all white, privileged and/or incessantly horny because, reasons. Like that the book is written by a Brit whose closest association with the US, apparently, is that she watched an episode of Friends and the aforementioned Animal House.<br /><br />But all these nitpicks are, y'know, apparently superfluous to the FEELS and the HAWTNESS and the OMG SQUEE.<br /><br />And I suppose this is revenge for authors such as Raine Miller getting everything about life in London wrong. <br /><br />But here's the thing. I can't turn off my self-literacy respect. I just can't. Maybe others can, but I can't disregard the fact that I love to read and I love authors who care deeply about their stories and who work hard to craft them to the best of their ability. And when I read something like this, something so obviously slap-dashed together to cater to a hot market without any care for the reader's reading comprehension ability and need to suspend disbelief -<br /><br />- I see red.<br /><br />So, SRSLY, authors, DO SOME BLOODY FUCKING RESEARCH in your haste to join the Great New Adult Money Grab Rush.<br /><br />DNF. I lived in the UK. If I wanted to be around Brits who get everything about life in the US wrong but think they know everything because they watched an hour or two of telly, I would have stayed there. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13231964388950127668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/744377305?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Christy by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle">Jennifer Kyle</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer744377305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16133068846584030762"><b>5 *Lucky Kiss* stars!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/c8d6eac3-9e66-40f1-aa81-0850f158f4b1_zps1d71b8e7.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406835570i/10605021.jpg' alt=' photo c8d6eac3-9e66-40f1-aa81-0850f158f4b1_zps1d71b8e7.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>When more than one friend tells me to read a book, and they all go on and on about how much they think I’ll love it, I really need to learn to listen. Otherwise, I’ll go months and months without reading that book, and when I finally do- I wonder why the heck it took so long. <i>Sweet Home</i> is that book for me. I have no idea why it took me so long to read it, but I’m so happy I did. It’s just the kind of book I needed. A sweet and fun tale of a modern day Romeo and his Moll</span>
  <span id="freeText16133068846584030762" style="display:none"><b>5 *Lucky Kiss* stars!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/c8d6eac3-9e66-40f1-aa81-0850f158f4b1_zps1d71b8e7.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406835570i/10605021.jpg" alt=" photo c8d6eac3-9e66-40f1-aa81-0850f158f4b1_zps1d71b8e7.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>When more than one friend tells me to read a book, and they all go on and on about how much they think I’ll love it, I really need to learn to listen. Otherwise, I’ll go months and months without reading that book, and when I finally do- I wonder why the heck it took so long. <i>Sweet Home</i> is that book for me. I have no idea why it took me so long to read it, but I’m so happy I did. It’s just the kind of book I needed. A sweet and fun tale of a modern day Romeo and his Molly Juliet. <br><br>Molly Juliet Shakespeare is a twenty year old student from England. She’s followed one of her professors from Oxford to Alabama to get her masters degree. Molly is fantastically nerdy and lovable. She’s not the most social or popular girl. She’s spent most of her life alone, losing much of her family young. She captured my heart from the first time she shouted Fuck wearing orange crocks. <br><i>
  <blockquote>Even in the vocabulary-rich world of academia, sometimes only the word “fuck” will suffice.</blockquote>
</i><br>Romeo Prince is the bad boy/football star of the campus. He doesn’t do girlfriends. He does hookups. He plays football and works hard at school to try to please his difficult parents. When he meets Molly, he is taken by her. There is something about this girl with the crazy hair, glasses, and english accent that makes him want her. <br><br>It all starts with a good luck kiss….<br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/d2352e4d-cdad-499b-bf67-9590b786934c_zpse9db493e.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406835570i/10605022.jpg" alt=" photo d2352e4d-cdad-499b-bf67-9590b786934c_zpse9db493e.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Once Rome has had a taste of Molly, he wants more. Molly has experienced so much loss in her life, she finds it difficult to get close to anyone. But Rome breaks through her walls. He cares for her and she feels more for him than she’s ever felt for anyone. What Rome loves best about Molly is that he can be himself with her. She see’s the real him and she loves him of who he is. <br><i>
  <blockquote>I like the way you are with me. I like me when I’m with you. I feel like I could tell you anythin’, that I could bear my fuckin’ black soul. You make me feel… well… you know…. You get me?” <br>“I get you, Romeo.”</blockquote>
</i><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/8c7d6204-83ac-476d-a100-9176f2f15730_zps4484186f.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406835570i/10605023.jpg" alt=" photo 8c7d6204-83ac-476d-a100-9176f2f15730_zps4484186f.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Rome is such a swoony hero! He’s sweet with Molly, but he’s also little broody, protective, possessive and all kinds of sexy.<br><i>
  <blockquote>“Not at all, Shakespeare, but hear this. I’m gonna fuck you, but I’m also gonna make love to you. I’m gonna own every goddamn piece of your soul, and I’m never gonna let you go. You’re gonna scream my name over and over until it’s permanently lodged in your friggin’ throat. You’re not gonna be just a fuck to me, Mol—you’re gonna be my fuckin’ salvation!” </blockquote>
</i><br>Molly is that fun, feisty and geeky girl that you can’t help but love. She’s smart and kind, someone you want to be your very best friend. I couldn’t help but love both of these main characters 100% of the time! <br><br>This couple couldn’t be more different on the outside, but when you really take a good look at them- they’re more alike than you would think. They bring out the best in each other. It was more than just an attraction between them. It went deeper than that. Rome and Molly had a connection. They understood each other, respected each other and just got one another. <br><br>I loved all the Romeo and Juliet comparisons and how the story was thrown together. It had just enough drama and angst to keep me on my toes, but it wasn’t an angst overload. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/7cb9ca76-53d2-489f-a31d-12972263e8da_zpsf44916b4.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406835570i/10605024.jpg" alt=" photo 7cb9ca76-53d2-489f-a31d-12972263e8da_zpsf44916b4.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Sweet Home</i> may not be the most original story I’ve ever read, but it’s a book that I devoured and thoroughly enjoyed. It’s the first Tillie Cole book I’ve had the pleasure of reading, but it won’t be my last! Romeo and Molly were such endearing characters. I adored everything about this fabulous couple. Overall, light and fun but it did have it’s heartbreaking moments. If you’re looking for a college aged NA book, pick this one up- It was fantastic! <br><i>
  <blockquote> “A home is not a place. It’s not a country or a town or a building or possession. Home is with the other half of your soul, the person who shares in your grief and helps you carry the burden of loss. Home is with the person who throughout it all never gives up on you and brings you eternal happiness.” </blockquote>
</i><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%205/d92ca782-dc48-4153-9449-4900566b32fb_zpsfeef557d.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406835570i/10605025.jpg" alt=" photo d92ca782-dc48-4153-9449-4900566b32fb_zpsfeef557d.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“It only took Romeo one look at Juliet and his fate was sealed. Maybe I’m just like my namesake, and maybe you’re just like yours.”<br>
</blockquote>
  </i>
</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7196126884073165929"><b>3 1/2 to 4–Made Me Smile–Stars.</b><br/><br/><i>Sweet Home</i> is the type of New Adult romance that would normally drive me nuts but ended up capturing my heart instead. Sure, there were some over-the-top, cheesy, and contrived moments that I couldn't help but roll my eyes at, but I rolled them with a HUGE, CHEESY GRIN ON MY FACE AND LOVING EVERY MINUTE OF IT.<br/><br/>I had so much fun reading this book. I loved the love story, the light and youthful feel, the angst that didn't feel too angsty, the playful humor, the heartb</span>
  <span id="freeText7196126884073165929" style="display:none"><b>3 1/2 to 4–Made Me Smile–Stars.</b><br /><br /><i>Sweet Home</i> is the type of New Adult romance that would normally drive me nuts but ended up capturing my heart instead. Sure, there were some over-the-top, cheesy, and contrived moments that I couldn't help but roll my eyes at, but I rolled them with a HUGE, CHEESY GRIN ON MY FACE AND LOVING EVERY MINUTE OF IT.<br /><br />I had so much fun reading this book. I loved the love story, the light and youthful feel, the angst that didn't feel too angsty, the playful humor, the heartbreaking moments, the possessive hero with a vulnerable side, and the sweetest, quirkiest, heroine I've read to date. I adored Molly. She's a New Adult heroine that's unique, a-dork-able, and a breath of fresh air. <br /><br />I read to escape and this book gave me just that...a great escape. I can't ask for more than that. </span>

<div id="review_743401184" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/743401184" />
    <a title="Patrycja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6852653-patrycja"><img alt="Patrycja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586460589p2/6852653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/743401184?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrycja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrycja" href="/user/show/6852653-patrycja">Patrycja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of sweet, hot romance novels with alpha males</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Patrycja by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/17969998-angelina">Angelina</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6852653-patrycja?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6852653-patrycja?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6852653-patrycja?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer743401184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14700780215042655744"><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>
      <i>"I don’t remember Romeo being this pushy with Juliet!”<br/>He arched his eyebrows meaningfully. “And look at how that worked out for them. My way is better—less death, more orgasms.” </i>
    </u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I devoured Sweet Home - this magical, adorable and extremely hot novel - so, so quickly, that I regret not doing it slower, only to enjoy it longer. I wish this book never ended. After reading few chapters, I felt glued to the pages, my heart started beating faster and I couldn’t make the silly gr</span>
  <span id="freeText14700780215042655744" style="display:none"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>
      <i>"I don’t remember Romeo being this pushy with Juliet!”<br>He arched his eyebrows meaningfully. “And look at how that worked out for them. My way is better—less death, more orgasms.” </i>
    </u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I devoured Sweet Home - this magical, adorable and extremely hot novel - so, so quickly, that I regret not doing it slower, only to enjoy it longer. I wish this book never ended. After reading few chapters, I felt glued to the pages, my heart started beating faster and I couldn’t make the silly grin disapear from my face. It was so, so good! <br><br>This story is so unique and refreshing. Roller coaster ride full of twist and turns, Sweet Home is intense , full of action passionate read that can be finished in one sitting. You will read it while biting your nails, laughing hard, wiping tears and fighting with lady boner.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382093682i/5659706._SX540_.jpg" width="400" alt="image" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is a story of Romeo Prince, twenty-one year old Quarterback - broody, sexy and possesive alpha male - that doesn’t take no for an answer. As a college star and extremely rich son of owner of oil plantations, Rome should feel like the king of the world, but his life is far from being perfect. Romeo suffers from cruel, controlling and demanding parents that treat him badly. Every day is a constant fight for being himself, when they want from him something else entirely. Living with a great responsability of being the best football player and fame makes it even harder for him to be free.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>
      <i>A small smile transformed his normally hardened features and he took my hand and ran it across his ribs. “Are they all there?” I frowned. “What?”<br>“My ribs. Is there one missin’?”<br>My hand smoothed up and down his sides. “Okay, I think you’ve lost it. You think you’re missing a rib?”<br>He exhaled a quiet laugh. “Just thought God took one of mine when he made you.” </i>
    </u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382093682i/5659707.jpg" width="400" alt="image" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Molly Juliet Shakespeare is a totall geek. In her nerd glasses, English accent and doing her master’s while being only twenty, doesn’t make her the most social person. Add to the mix that growning up wasn’t easy for her – first she lost her mother, few years after that her father and then grandma, Molly is completely alone in the big world. <br>When she finally meets Romeo her lone life changes. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>
      <i> „I get so lonely that at times, I literally think it might kill me.”<br>Devastation engulfed his features and he rolled on top of me, urgently pressing his mouth on my lips, on my cheeks, on my forehead. “Molly, baby, you’re breakin’ my fuckin’ heart.”<br>“It’s true and I’ve never told anyone that until just now… until you. For me, it’s been the hardest thing. It’s amazing how loud the sound of silence can be screaming at you relentlessly, reminding you that you’re completely on your own in the world.”<br>Romeo licked his bottom lip anxiously and his eyes began to glisten. “Can I tell you somethin’?”<br>I nodded shyly. He ran his finger down my cheek, but almost as if the action fuelled his strength rather than gave me comfort. “I’m desperately lonely, too.” </i>
    </u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382093682i/5659708.jpg" width="400" alt="image" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Romeo, sigh, Romeo! He is the perfect example of alpha male and the characteristics I crave in my men. Possesive, yet caring, sweet and gentle when the situation begs for it and rough, controlling when the time’s right. He made everything so freaking hot! Sex scenes were out of this world and the connection he had with Molly only made it so much better! <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>
      <i>“Not at all, Shakespeare, but hear this. I’m gonna fuck you, but I’m also gonna make love to you. I’m gonna own every goddamn piece of your soul, and I’m never gonna let you go. You’re gonna scream my name over and over until it’s permanently lodged in your friggin’ throat. You’re not gonna be just a fuck to me, Mol—you’re gonna be my fuckin’ salvation!” </i>
    </u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I have no idea how to describe how much I adored this book. It’s impossible. Sweet Home is a perfect mix of sweetness, pain and deep love. Step by step, page by page I slowly fell in love with this complex bittersweet story. I live for surprises like this! When I don’t know what the story will be like and then when I finally start to read it, and it melts my heart, make me swoon and enjoy it very much, I’m the happiest person in the whole world. <br><br>Overall, I’m in need to find my own Romeo, and not the one Shakespeare wrote about. I need my own Romeo Prince. Sweet Home is fantastic book and I can’t wait to read and sweet what else Tilli Cole, can come up with. I highly recommend this book for every fan of sexy new adult books. <br></span>

<div id="review_748311907" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/748311907" />
    <a title="Karla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3117503-karla"><img alt="Karla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383769554p2/3117503.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/748311907?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karla" href="/user/show/3117503-karla">Karla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3117503-karla?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3117503-karla?shelf=waste-of-time">waste-of-time</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer748311907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4719326060675412443">There is nothing more I dislike than not finishing a book. Especially one that I spent money on. And more than $0.99. Sadly, this is a book that I couldn’t even force myself through half of to try to justify the money spent. <br/>A couple of my sticking points:<br/><blockquote>1. Write what you know. If you haven’t spent a significant amount of time in the south, don’t write about the south. Droppin’ the ‘g’ off any word endin’ with an “ing” and addin’ in ‘ain’t' every few words doesn’t make a realistic dialogue. It </blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText4719326060675412443" style="display:none">There is nothing more I dislike than not finishing a book. Especially one that I spent money on. And more than $0.99. Sadly, this is a book that I couldn’t even force myself through half of to try to justify the money spent. <br />A couple of my sticking points:<br /><blockquote>1. Write what you know. If you haven’t spent a significant amount of time in the south, don’t write about the south. Droppin’ the ‘g’ off any word endin’ with an “ing” and addin’ in ‘ain’t' every few words doesn’t make a realistic dialogue. It makes for an annoying one. This could have been a decent book, but every time I saw the missing ‘g,’ I got distracted. I’m pretty sure you wanted to write about a southern boy and thought “oh, all southerners skip the ‘g’, it’s perfect!” That would be the equivalent of me adding in bloody every other bloody word and considering myself bloody English. In choosing to write a book where the character needs a strong regional dialect, either spend the time to get it right, or place the book in a locale where it comes naturally.</blockquote><br /><blockquote>2. Show me the money! Or in this case, the emotions. Scenes were so much more about telling vs showing that they didn’t make sense. Romeo’s anger never came across and it was so confusing. I only figured out he was angry when Pollyanna let us know “He was angry/mad/upset/brooding/pissed off.” Half the time I read a scene, then Molly would say something – comment on his alpha, take-charge, no-shit attitude, or the like – and I would just be left stumped. Because what I’d just read wasn’t an alpha, take-charge, no-shit attitude.</blockquote><br /><blockquote>3. There is no chemistry at all. With anyone. With Shakespear and Romeo. With Shakespear and her friends. </blockquote><br /><blockquote>4. Peripheral characters were just that – grossly exaggerated caricatures of people. They don’t come across as real, they don’t come across as having any kind of relationship, and they don’t add any value. Although, this gem was wonderful: ‘What’s up, bitches? Are we headin’ to this jig or what? I want to see what prime beef is on offer? Mamma’s taco needs a good ol’ fillin’.’ Let’s just digest this line for a few seconds. It really could have been an example in point 1, but I digress. She’s southern, so of course, she’s missin’ her ‘g’, and we even went so far as to get rid of the ‘d’ on ol’. But a jig? I don’t think I’ve ever heard anyone in America refer to a party as a jig. And the constant references to the fat girl were just annoying. Why do we need to know everything that she’s eating? </blockquote><br />If there were any way to get my money or my time back, I would be putting in a request for a refund on both. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4719326060675412443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_707391603" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/707391603" />
    <a title="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog"><img alt="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429608146p2/12994342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/707391603?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" href="/user/show/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog">Smitten&#39;s Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=steamy-reads">steamy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=emotional-reads">emotional-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=angst-filled-reads">angst-filled-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=bad-boy">bad-boy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=alpha-male">alpha-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=domestic-child-abuse">domestic-child-abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=sports-star-hero">sports-star-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=college-romance">college-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=hea">hea</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer707391603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17452561782335079004"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536675i/5968034._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536675i/5968035._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I love this author!<br/><br/><b>5 stars for Romeo Prince and Molly <i>Juliet</i> Shakespeare!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536675i/5968036._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Hey, Mol."<br/>"Hey, you."<br/>"You gonna give up that sweet kiss?"<br/>"If that's what you want."<br/>"It definitely is."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Whilst there are threads from Shakespeare's Romeo and Juliet throughout this book, <i>Sweet Home</i>, it is not just a modern day Romeo and Juliet. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536830i/5968190.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Molly is a twenty year old brainiac. She's super smart, studious and sensible. With no family and no ties, working-class, English good-girl, Molly Shakespeare leaves Engla</span>
  <span id="freeText17452561782335079004" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536675i/5968034._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536675i/5968035._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love this author!<br><br><b>5 stars for Romeo Prince and Molly <i>Juliet</i> Shakespeare!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536675i/5968036._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Hey, Mol."<br>"Hey, you."<br>"You gonna give up that sweet kiss?"<br>"If that's what you want."<br>"It definitely is."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Whilst there are threads from Shakespeare's Romeo and Juliet throughout this book, <i>Sweet Home</i>, it is not just a modern day Romeo and Juliet. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536830i/5968190.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Molly is a twenty year old brainiac. She's super smart, studious and sensible. With no family and no ties, working-class, English good-girl, Molly Shakespeare leaves England to study her masters in philosophy at the University of Alabama.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536675i/5968037.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"I came to college to study, Cass, not to whore myself out to drunken frat boys!"<br>She gaffawed. "Whatever, darlin', you won't be thinking of studying when your ankles are wrapped 'round some stud's neck as he wears you like a necklace, tickling your belly button from the inside!"</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Dangerously handsome, twenty one year old, bad-boy, Romeo Prince is the star quarterback for Crimson Tide. His successful future in football is a dead cert and he's 'Bama's hero. Woo! Roll Tide! But his cruel, controlling, oil tycoon parents have other ideas. Ideas of him taking on the family business and marrying their version of his perfect suitor.<br>Molly has no clue about crimson Tide, or quarterbacks, or anything football related, for that matter. She doesn't know that Romeo is notorious, or that he is unattainable and dangerously moody. She just knows that he's devestatingly good looking and that he makes her heart race. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"He's standoffish, all moody and dark, but more importantly, he's the friggin' starting QB for the tide!"<br>"Official statistics - six foot three, two-hundred and thirty-five pounds of solid muscle!" Cass added excitedly.<br>"He's a what? For who?"</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536675i/5968038.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Romeo and Molly meet, both their worlds change completely. But can these two 'star crossed lovers' find a way for their completely different worlds to work together?<br><br>I was a huge fan of Tillie Cole's previous novel, rom-com movie star romance, <i>Eternally North</i>. (Check it out if you haven't already)<br>So when she asked me to read <i>Sweet Home</i>, I jumped at the chance. And it didn't disappoint. Again, there was some light hearted humour, a whole lot of swoon-worthy romance and also some heavier, juicier threads to the plot-line, too, adding extra depth to an otherwise sweet, cutesy romance.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536675i/5968039._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's a fairly typical bad-boy falls for good-girl story. There's a lot of them about, but I just can't get enough of them. There is something fundamentally adorable about a big hulking badass guy who suddenly exposes his soft, gooey, sensitive centre for the girl of his dreams. Don't lie, we all want that bad-boy who turns good just for li'l old us! It's the ultimate romantic fantasy for most girls. And that's exactly what you get with <i>Sweet Home</i>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You, Molly Shakespeare, have just publicly made out with the most desirable guy on campus. A guy that never commits to anyone. A guy that other guys are shit scared of and girls would gladly give a lung for."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Romeo is a super talented sportsman. He's ripped, fast, gifted and has a very quick temper. He has the obligatory tortured past, dysfunctional family and anger issues, to boot. He's lonely and broken and you can't help but want to fix him. Of course, he hides his scars beneath his man-whoring facade, sleeping with every girl that throws themselves at his feet. That is, until he falls hard and fast for geeky, glasses-wearing Molly.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Why does any human want anyone? My body recognises you as something that's good for me. My mind recognises you as someone who's right for me, and my soul recognises you as someone who is meant for me."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536675i/5968040._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Molly is the ultimate goody-two-shoes. <i>Sweet Home</i> is told from her point of view, so you really get to witness her transformation throughout the book, as she discovers the girl behind the glasses. When we meet Molly, she's not a fan of parties, she can count her friends on one hand and she has only ever had sex once. Oh, and she wears bright orange Crocs. 'Nuff said! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536675i/5968041._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But don't panic, she isn't irritating and in denial about her feelings for Romeo. She quickly realises that she's attracted to him and is curious to explore those feelings, despite the fact that they scare her a little and push her out of her comfort zone. She's a great heroine and I really enjoyed reading her.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536675i/5968042._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved the comparisons to Shakespeare's <i>Romeo and Juliet</i>. They were well written and comical, in a way that Tillie Cole almost pokes fun at the parallels between the two stories in some parts.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"It only took Romeo one look at Juliet and his fate was sealed. Maybe I'm just like my namesake, and maybe you're just like yours."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>There are some very steamy sex scenes and Romeo is super controlling, super alpha. At times, I felt that he veered a little away from dominant, toward annoyingly bossy and a little aggressive, but for the most part, it was extremely hot!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"I don't remember Romeo being this pushy with Juliet!"<br>He arched his eyebrows meaningfully. "And look at how that worked out for them. My way is better - less death, more orgasms."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I loved that these character filled a void for one another throughout this story. Both Molly and Romeo are cripplingly lonely and they find solace, comfort and companionship in each other. I really felt that connection between them, and I felt that their bond was that much stronger because they each understood one another's pain and craved the support that the other could offer them. So heart warming.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"I get so lonely that at times, I literally think it might kill me."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536675i/5968043.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Despite a relatively light-hearted, fun feel throughout the majority of this book, it does deal with some deep, intense issues. There are some heavy, upsetting scenes and I did shed a few tears. Read my 'warnings' at the end of this review if you are easily effected by emotional triggers. However, Tillie Cole did a great job of conveying the emotional trauma and of piecing her characters back together at the end of the book.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Molly, a home is not a place. It's not a country or a town or a building or possession. Home is with the other half of your soul, the person who shares your grief and helps you carry the burden of loss. Home is with the person who throughout it all never gives up on you and brings you eternal happiness. That, Molly dear, is your home sweet home."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I would highly recommend Tillie Cole's books. She's fantastic at writing stories with a little bit of everything in. Her books are sweet, romantic, sexy, funny and gripping. She's incredibly talented at being able to create stories that will not only have you giggling and swooning throughout, but also have depth and emotion, too.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1382536675i/5968044._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><i>Sweet Home</i> Statistics</b><br><b>Steam Rating (out of 5):</b> ♥♥♥♥<br><b>Ending:</b> Happy Ending<br><b>Series:</b> ✗ <br><b>Can this be read as a standalone?</b> Yes<br><b>Themes:</b><br>Football<br>Bad boy/good girl<br>Abusive parents<br>Grief<br><b>Warning. This book includes...</b> <br>Sexual content. Miscarriage. Violence.<br><b>Writing:</b> Great<br><br><a href="http://www.amazon.co.uk/Sweet-Home-Tillie-Cole-ebook/dp/B00FVMDQ30/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1382449658&amp;sr=8-1&amp;keywords=sweet+home+tillie+cole" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392852i/756313._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://www.amazon.com/Sweet-Home-Tillie-Cole-ebook/dp/B00FVMDQ30/ref=sr_1_1?ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1382449658&amp;sr=8-1&amp;keywords=sweet+home+tillie+cole" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392852i/756314._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/744646354?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="* Meli Mel *" class="user" itemprop="url" name="* Meli Mel *" href="/user/show/10905711-meli-mel">* Meli Mel *</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer744646354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer406287891740970964"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400128i/775030._SX540_.jpg' width='125' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>♥ ♥ ♥ 4 STARS ♥ ♥ ♥</b><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433629482i/15123224._SY540_.png' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br/><br/>“Hey, Mol”<br/>“Hey, you.”<br/>“You going to give up that lucky sweet kiss?”<br/>“If that’s what you want.”<br/>“It most definitely is.”<br/><br/>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422597725i/13523034._SX540_.gif' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Molly Shakespeare has had quite the life at just twenty years old. It has been tragic for her, and now she wants to a new start. She leaves England to go to the University of Alabama. Adjusting to the american life is a bit of a struggle for her, but her ne</span>
  <span id="freeText406287891740970964" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400128i/775030._SX540_.jpg" width="125" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>♥ ♥ ♥ 4 STARS ♥ ♥ ♥</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433629482i/15123224._SY540_.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>“Hey, Mol”<br>“Hey, you.”<br>“You going to give up that lucky sweet kiss?”<br>“If that’s what you want.”<br>“It most definitely is.”<br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422597725i/13523034._SX540_.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Molly Shakespeare has had quite the life at just twenty years old. It has been tragic for her, and now she wants to a new start. She leaves England to go to the University of Alabama. Adjusting to the american life is a bit of a struggle for her, but her new found friends are eager to take her under their wing and teach her how to experience life. Another thing that has Molly clueless is how much these people of Alabama love football. She just doesn't get it. When she meets the star quarterback, Rome Prince, she can't help but feel attracted to him. She just has no idea who exactly Rome Prince is or how he will impact her life.<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1405682320ra/10435311.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br> <br>“He’s not just a football player. He’s the bravest, most caring person I’ve ever met. He understands me like no one before. He’s my soul mate—he’s my everything.”<br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br>Molly Shakespeare was somewhat of an introvert. She enjoys reading and studying. She has been on her own for quite some time so she has become accustomed to her solitude. When she arrives in America she realizes that it will change for her. She makes friends very outgoing girls that thrust her into the sorority life. I liked that just because she seemed quiet on the outside she could defend herself when she needed to. She was intelligent, caring, and just overall very likable. The poor girl didn't stand a chance when it came to Rome Prince. Holy smokes was he hot! He was super alpha and it drove me nuts how much that melted me. I seriously loved the guy. He doesn't have the best of upbringings either, which is how Molly and him connected even deeper. They understood what it was like to feel alone. And because of their connection, they inevitably fall for each other.<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433629901ra/15123295.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●<br><br>"Home is with the other half of your soul, the person who shares your grief and helps you carry the burden of loss. Home is with the person who throughout it all never gives up on you and brings you eternal happiness. That, Molly dear, is your home sweet home."<br><br>●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●  ●</b>
</blockquote><br>This story was über sweet, just like it says in the name. I really enjoyed this one and loved the main characters. Despite it being really sweet it wasn't complete fluff, there were some sad parts that really pulled at my heart strings. There was also a bit of angst to keep things interesting. I could not believe how awful Rome was treated by his parents. I just loathed them. I was so glad he finally had someone that cared for him in Molly. Molly and Rome were so perfect for each other, they may have had their flaws, but that didn't affect how much I liked them. The only reason I am not giving this 5 stars is because it was crazy cheesy and a tad bit predictable. However, I couldn't help but love either way. It was a great romantic read. Now, if only I can find a real life Rome Prince.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422597725i/13523034._SX540_.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="406287891740970964" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15694612227067513180">4.5--<b>SWEET and SEXY</b>--Stars!!!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403968ra/785981.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I am seriously swooning over here! I don't know what it was--timing or what--but this book was just what I was looking for. I really, really loved it!!! <br/><br/>Sweet Home is the story of <b>Romeo</b> Prince and Molly <b>Juliet</b> Shakespeare. Now don't go running for the hills....Molly and Romeo's story was so-so sweet. They melted my heart. And made me smile. And giggle like a love-sick school girl! LMAO!<br/><br/>Molly, 20 has landed in Alabama by way of England (yup, she's British--LOVE). She'</span>
  <span id="freeText15694612227067513180" style="display:none">4.5--<b>SWEET and SEXY</b>--Stars!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403968ra/785981.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I am seriously swooning over here! I don't know what it was--timing or what--but this book was just what I was looking for. I really, really loved it!!! <br><br>Sweet Home is the story of <b>Romeo</b> Prince and Molly <b>Juliet</b> Shakespeare. Now don't go running for the hills....Molly and Romeo's story was so-so sweet. They melted my heart. And made me smile. And giggle like a love-sick school girl! LMAO!<br><br>Molly, 20 has landed in Alabama by way of England (yup, she's British--LOVE). She's studying for her Master's. She's quirky, different, brainy. She meets Romeo on the first day of classes. Romeo is the starting QB for the Crimson Tide. He's aloof, angry, moody, man-whore. He's intrigued by Molly. <br><br>Romeo, Romeo, Romeo.....<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381949473ra/5462045.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Romeo was bloody brilliant. He was possessive and demanding and RAWR but at the same time sweet and protective and loving. It was the perfect mix. But he was so broken and damaged from his GAWD awful parents.<br><br>Romeo's mom...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381950949ra/5464061.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/629472.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Not to mention that BITCH Shelly, don't even get me started on her. UGH! <br><br>I loved the supporting characters--Molly's tobacco spittin' roomate Cass especially. She was hilarious! <br><br>Really there wasn't a ton of angst in this book. At least nothing too stupid and annoying. There were a few cheesy bits but nothing that took away from the story. Romeo and Molly were super HOT together...Romeo in the bedroom.....HOLY MOLY GUACAMOLE!!!! I need a Romeo. <br><br>I loved their football game "kiss" tradition. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381951256ra/5464582.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>SO sweet! I just loved Romeo and Molly....everything about them. They were two broken people who found "home" with each other. <br><br></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10247668-katy-loves-romance?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10247668-katy-loves-romance?shelf=bad-boys">bad-boys</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1155997459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5225320990830805195"> <b>5 "Hey Mol, Hey you" Stars*****</b><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>First of all what a whirlwind I have lived breathed inhaled and LOVED every Goddamn word and sentence this story has given me, I mean why haven't I read any of Tillies books before? What an Idiot... anyway I digress you get it I loved this whole story with A BANG actually sports romance is a genre I adore it's one of those stories where I can get away from life and delve into and really remember university life being younger with no responsibilities as such but</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText5225320990830805195" style="display:none"> <b>5 "Hey Mol, Hey you" Stars*****</b><br><br><br><b>
  <i>First of all what a whirlwind I have lived breathed inhaled and LOVED every Goddamn word and sentence this story has given me, I mean why haven't I read any of Tillies books before? What an Idiot... anyway I digress you get it I loved this whole story with A BANG actually sports romance is a genre I adore it's one of those stories where I can get away from life and delve into and really remember university life being younger with no responsibilities as such but mainly its sweet, fun a whole lot of sexy and this one has a stack on emotion in the mix which MADE ME FELL!!! Gah sorry this review is going to be slightly soppy 'I apologise'</i>
</b> <br><br><br><a href="http://s1298.photobucket.com/user/ktdunning/media/book%20collages/F1BB04CE-24CF-4347-B79B-20B98F8E45CD_zpsvxew4zxf.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420679107i/13252187._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo F1BB04CE-24CF-4347-B79B-20B98F8E45CD_zpsvxew4zxf.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><b>So What's it about?</b><br>Molly Shakespeare is studious she delves into books and works hard cause she learnt at a young age what its like to be lonely she runs away from anything that will allow her to get near anyone else just in case that person gets taken away from her again. Her mum died at birth her dad died when she was 6 and then her gran who she adored and brought her up died when she was 14 leaving her in foster care we know that's not always the best therefore she has brought herself up she stands on her own two feet and with her head held high, but she doesn't let people in greatly until she meets Romeo. <br><br><br>Romeo hasn't had the best upbringing with cold hearted parents who only care about money and their reputation it doesn't matter about his goals or aspirations or what he wants with <b>his</b> life that's what they want for him to be the dutiful son, but Romeo is the Best Quarterback in town he's a born leader and loves his team, but due to his upbringing he doesn't let people in either apart from his cousin who he adores and his only release is women lots of them but they don't know his heart nor anything other than the player that he is. <br><br><br>But one class is all it takes to find each other and find something that pulls at their seams they just can't seem to walk away from each other. This is very much a story about two people who are from two different worlds who find something in each other that gives them hope and ultimately love which is what they both deep down crave~ <b>to be loved.</b> <br><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Why am I more? I don't get it." "You just are. You somehow give me peace in my completely fucked-up world. you get me; no one has before. It's that simple."</blockquote>
</b><br><br><br>They understand each other like no-one else has they've been so closed off from feeling and letting anyone in that when they see each other THEY KNOW! <br><br><br><b>This is also a story about firsts!!!</b><br><a href="http://s1298.photobucket.com/user/ktdunning/media/book%20collages/2729D6B5-9643-4E89-A85B-A1E8D7A6324B_zpsqrcmymap.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420679107i/13252188._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 2729D6B5-9643-4E89-A85B-A1E8D7A6324B_zpsqrcmymap.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Touches and kisses.<br><a href="http://s1298.photobucket.com/user/ktdunning/media/kissing/kissing%20gif%202_zpstfmnjve6.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420679107ra/13252189.gif" alt=" photo kissing gif 2_zpstfmnjve6.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Romeo is the Quarterback he loves his team it's what he strives to be, he loves it he's good at it but his parents don't approve and while he loves it he has to be careful with the people he cares about which is why he's never let anyone in. This book has a level of angst to it, I was biting my nails at the later end of the book when I realised or guessed what was happening. Romeo is Intense and when he loves and lets in he loves HARD and HARD he loves his girl his lucky girl who he needs to protect and he'll do anything in his power to do that. <br><br><br><a href="http://s1298.photobucket.com/user/ktdunning/media/book%20collages/3481A8B0-7413-4AF4-B679-2635AC8717F3_zpsywxyfp7k.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420679107i/13252190._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 3481A8B0-7413-4AF4-B679-2635AC8717F3_zpsywxyfp7k.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><b>My Thoughts</b><br>I loved it, it kept me on my toes I was ahhing when they first kissed, I was jumping for joy when they got down to it I mean those scenes blew me away, <b>Intense sexy emotional</b> and I had tears in my eyes on many quotes I highlighted a lot. Rome is everything I want in an hero he's Strong, he wants to dominate in the bedroom its where he seeks control its what he needs, where his parents never aloud it in his life he does there and he does on the field. He's a born leader as explained throughout my review but he is also sweet and he melted my heart, he has a BIG OLE HEART I really don't know anyone who couldn't love his soul and I really will be thinking about him for days. <br><br>Molly is Independent, slightly geeky but opposites attract and that was for sure with these pair I instantly felt their attraction, their chemistry <b>THEM</b>. She is also strong but they ultimately needed each other and together they were heart warming, lovely, sexy I really don't want to stop reading them so going to now read Sweet Rome. <br><br><br><a href="http://s1298.photobucket.com/user/ktdunning/media/book%20collages/CD983C54-9B9D-438A-B570-B8DC9A530ED4_zpsbutwwtzj.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420679107i/13252191._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo CD983C54-9B9D-438A-B570-B8DC9A530ED4_zpsbutwwtzj.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><b>Thanks for reading my gushing soppy review sorry again~ That is all</b><br><br><b>For more Reviews, cover reveals Blog posts and Giveaways you can follow our blog here!!</b><br><a href="http://slutsistas.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1417650623i/12469037._SX540_.png" height="90" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8068927679414781278"> <b>5 “You’re my home” Stars. </b><br/>	<br/>Sometimes when I read a book, I’m lucky enough to think when I end it: “Why did it take me so long to read this??!”. This was exactly what happened for me in this one. I thought why it took almost a year for me to read this. <br/>Because, my friends, this book is a majestically written and beautiful love story. I’ve cried, I smiled, I laughed and I felt my heart warming through the whole book. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415055142i/11720088._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Lonely Molly just arrived at college in Alabama to finish her masters. Alone in </span>
  <span id="freeText8068927679414781278" style="display:none"> <b>5 “You’re my home” Stars. </b><br>	<br>Sometimes when I read a book, I’m lucky enough to think when I end it: “Why did it take me so long to read this??!”. This was exactly what happened for me in this one. I thought why it took almost a year for me to read this. <br>Because, my friends, this book is a majestically written and beautiful love story. I’ve cried, I smiled, I laughed and I felt my heart warming through the whole book. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415055142i/11720088._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lonely Molly just arrived at college in Alabama to finish her masters. Alone in life she’s used to solitude so she really doesn’t expect to fall in love. <br>And she especially doesn’t expect the receiving end of her love to be Romeo Prince, the sexy and all-star quarterback of their college. <br>And what she really didn’t expect? For him to be as broken and lonely and her. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415055142i/11720089.jpg" width="350" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Romeo is beautiful, rich, and popular and everyone knows he’ll be signed to play professionally. What everyone doesn’t know is that his parents keep ruining him and his life and although he’s surrounded of people who worship him, he’s alone in the world most of the time. <br>So when sweet, innocent and British Molly, who doesn’t know a thing about football and is as alone as himself, he can’t help but following in love.<br>They are both searching for somewhere to belong, and they find out that maybe they’re each other’s home. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415055142i/11720090.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But when his parents start to interfere, crazy ex-girlfriend enter the picture, their pasts and everyone around them (including the media) are lurking in every corner, they find their path to happiness, can be rougher than they ever thought. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1402872274i/10002999.jpg" width="350" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <b>Rating: </b> 5 Stars. <br> <b>Characters Development: </b> I loved them both. Loved them individually, because Molly was so strong and yet, sweet and Rome was also all these things. Although slightly broken, he was a loyal and passionate hero that gave everything he had. I loved him. <br>This book also had an amazing group pf supportive characters, some of them, I can’t wait to hear their stories! <br> <b>Steam: </b> Hot. <br> <b>Sensible Subjects: </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Suicide.
