              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14302918-patty-wrapped-up-in-reading-book-blog?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer694541443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17096160630272532492">*****4.5 STARS*****<br/>(BR with Mel and Dee)<br/><br/><a href='http://s1276.photobucket.com/user/tennyspa/media/a59c7c8d5725add8c5857b58f256a5f1_zps98265525.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1410834719i/11158012._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo a59c7c8d5725add8c5857b58f256a5f1_zps98265525.jpg' width='340' height='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/><br/><b>"Sweet Home"</b> is sort of a modern day twist on the old tale of "Romeo & Juliet". Molly Juliet Shakespeare, is completing her Masters in Philosophy at The University of Alabama. She recently transferred from Oxford University in England and is also acting as a Research & Teacher's assistant to one of her Professors who has come to the University of Alabama as well. Molly has a past that is filled with so much heartbreak and is basically an orphan. When t</span>
  <span id="freeText17096160630272532492" style="display:none">*****4.5 STARS*****<br>(BR with Mel and Dee)<br><br><a href="http://s1276.photobucket.com/user/tennyspa/media/a59c7c8d5725add8c5857b58f256a5f1_zps98265525.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1410834719i/11158012._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo a59c7c8d5725add8c5857b58f256a5f1_zps98265525.jpg" width="340" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br><b>"Sweet Home"</b> is sort of a modern day twist on the old tale of "Romeo &amp; Juliet". Molly Juliet Shakespeare, is completing her Masters in Philosophy at The University of Alabama. She recently transferred from Oxford University in England and is also acting as a Research &amp; Teacher's assistant to one of her Professors who has come to the University of Alabama as well. Molly has a past that is filled with so much heartbreak and is basically an orphan. When things get too rough for her, she runs away from the situation.<br><br><br>Romeo Prince, it a senior at the University of Alabama and he is the Star Quarterback. He's known to have a bad boy reputation and he also has practically slept with most of the coeds on campus. He comes from old money and he also has a heartbreaking story.<br><br><br><a href="http://s1276.photobucket.com/user/tennyspa/media/bcb1cfbd4e987381b134c96c66999173_zpsef031d63.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1410834719i/11158013._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo bcb1cfbd4e987381b134c96c66999173_zpsef031d63.jpg" width="345" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br>When Molly and Rome meet there is an instant attraction and I have to say it was pretty much "insta-love". I know some times people hate when this happens in a story, but I think in some instances it is appropriate. In this story, I totally get how these two fell so hard, so fast. It happens some times. Two people just connect on a crazy level.<br>These two were made to love each other.<br><br><br><br>I adored Molly. She was the cute and nerdy British girl who wore orange crocs to class. Any girl who can rock a pair of crocs and not give a damn about what other people think, is pretty fabulous to me. I really felt for this poor girl. I can't even imagine losing everyone I loved and moving to a different country where I didn't have any family or friends. She was definitely a brave girl. Some times a little too naive, but all around a very lovable heroine.<br><br><br><br>Rome was a smokin' HOT, Alpha Male Football Quarterback!<br>I was hooked the moment these two ran into each other outside class, and won over when they first kiss during a Sorority Pledge hazing. His home life has been pretty atrocious. I can't even begin to describe how disgusting his parents were. They were so evil at times I thought it was just a bit <b>over the top.</b> But as I read on, I understood why the author wrote the story this way. <br><br><br>Not only is Rome the Star Quarterback, and the object of every girls'desire, he is also what I would call a Dominant. Now he's not a hardcore Dom, but he definitely makes sure he is the one in control when having sex. I had issues with this in the beginning. I am not a prude or against BDSM. I actually love reading BDSM stories. I would go so far as to say I'd even try some of it out. BUT, I thought it was quite odd to have this in the story. I really felt it didn't fit. As I read on, and learned about Rome's childhood and why his parents were always so evil to him, I understood his need for Control when it came to sex.<br><br><br>Rome and Molly will face obstacles.<br>Of course, you know they are not going to have an HEA early on in the story.<br>There is bound to be a thing or two that will threaten their relationship.<br>Some things had me screaming, and there were times I was close to tears.<br>I have to say I really just wanted Rome's mom to die a horrible death.<br><br><br><br>The sexy times, well hell, they were <b>INCREDIBLY HOT</b>!!!<br>It's why I've added Rome to my Top Fantasy Book Boyfriends list.<br>I mean this guy knows what he is doing and his Dom like behavior may have caused a few panty soaking moments.<br><br><br><br><a href="http://s1276.photobucket.com/user/tennyspa/media/4693ada9bddd1ddaae0d563e014df745_zps5e0fc2e7.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1410834719i/11158014._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 4693ada9bddd1ddaae0d563e014df745_zps5e0fc2e7.jpg" width="340" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br>I really enjoyed the book and at first I was going to rate this a 4, but towards the end, Rome just had my heart melting and so I went and changed it to a 4.5!! <br><br><br><i>
  <b>"For never was a truer story of love conquering woe than this of Molly Juliet and her Romeo."</b>
</i><br><br><br>I loved how it ended and am off to start "SWEET ROME" now!!<br><br></span>

<div id="review_785924171" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/785924171" />
    <a title="mich" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17575003-mich"><img alt="mich" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361178507p2/17575003.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/785924171?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mich" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mich" href="/user/show/17575003-mich">mich</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17575003-mich?shelf=this-book-is-stupid">this-book-is-stupid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17575003-mich?shelf=cheesy-corny-roll-eyes">cheesy-corny-roll-eyes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17575003-mich?shelf=dont-do-it">dont-do-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17575003-mich?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17575003-mich?shelf=sports">sports</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17575003-mich?shelf=will-not-try-this-author-again">will-not-try-this-author-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer785924171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12789535193722923541">I have only one real life friend who loves to read as much as I do (just one, isn't that crazy?! What the hell does everyone else <i>do</i> with their free time??) Anyway, every once in awhile she'll recommend a book to me that I absolutely MUST read and it always comes with her standard endorsement of "OMG this is the best book evarrrr!!!" Lol, I love her enthusiasm, and actually, I just plain love her to pieces. Problem is, I effing hate her book recs.<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>"What's up, bitches? Are we headin' to this ji</blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText12789535193722923541" style="display:none">I have only one real life friend who loves to read as much as I do (just one, isn't that crazy?! What the hell does everyone else <i>do</i> with their free time??) Anyway, every once in awhile she'll recommend a book to me that I absolutely MUST read and it always comes with her standard endorsement of "OMG this is the best book evarrrr!!!" Lol, I love her enthusiasm, and actually, I just plain love her to pieces. Problem is, I effing hate her book recs.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"What's up, bitches? Are we headin' to this jig or what? I wanna see what prime beef is on offer. Mama's taco needs a good ol' fillin'."</blockquote>
</i><br />If you think these are humorous, believable lines, then please by all means read this book. If, however, you thought that piece of dialogue was stupid as fuck (like I did), then I advise you to run away from this book – <i>fast.</i><br /><br />I lost count of how many times I screamed in my head, “WHO TALKS LIKE THIS?!?” Jesus, the dialogue was <i>awful</i>, terrible, fucking horrendous! NO ONE talks like these people, the whole thing was a total joke. Even if this had been the best plotted story, I still could not have liked it simply because of the dumbass dialogue. <br /><br />Also, this was not the best plotted story. Not even close. In case you couldn’t tell from the subtle hints in the blurb, Sweet Home is a story that appears to be inspired by William Shakespeare’s Romeo and Juliet. It makes me cringe to think that this well-known tale of star-crossed lovers has been used in any way whatsoever to inspire this piece of work laden with cheesy circumstances, stupid dialogue, and weak characterizations overflowing with over the top stereotypes. And Shakespeare is probably rolling over in his grave right now and wondering-- ok, I am so NOT gonna finish this sentence. I had typed out what I was thinking and realized it was too much, so I’m letting the delete key do its job. (I’ll just say it had to do with a taco and leave it at that.) <br /><br />This is the 3rd book in a row that my friend recommended to me that I hated, and I’m really sad that it seems like we’re starting to just have different tastes. In the past, we’ve had fierce love for several of the same books, like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13312527.The_Opportunist__Love_Me_with_Lies___1_" title="The Opportunist (Love Me with Lies, #1) by Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener">The Opportunist</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11500217.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days___1_" title="Angelfall (Penryn &amp; the End of Days, #1) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a>, but in the last year things have taken a different turn. (And it goes both ways too: she asked me why I hated her and if I was literally trying to kill her with boredom when I had her read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17332556.The_Burning_Sky__The_Elemental_Trilogy___1_" title="The Burning Sky (The Elemental Trilogy, #1) by Sherry Thomas" rel="nofollow noopener">The Burning Sky</a>, lol.) Oh well, all I can say is, thank god for goodreads.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12789535193722923541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_745887202" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/745887202" />
    <a title="Shell The Belle " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15880350-shell-the-belle"><img alt="Shell The Belle " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399759491p2/15880350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/745887202?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shell The Belle " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shell The Belle " href="/user/show/15880350-shell-the-belle">Shell The Belle </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15880350-shell-the-belle?shelf=guys-i-want-to-kick-in-the-balls">guys-i-want-to-kick-in-the-balls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15880350-shell-the-belle?shelf=what-the-hell-was-all-the-hype-for">what-the-hell-was-all-the-hype-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15880350-shell-the-belle?shelf=alpah-wannabe">alpah-wannabe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15880350-shell-the-belle?shelf=alpha-wannabe">alpha-wannabe</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer745887202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3174246805809220914"><b>My Review of SWEET HOME by Tilly Cole</b><br/><br/><b>1.5 stars, and that is for the beginning and the end. </b><br/><br/>Oops, I did it again – I fell for the hype, that is. <br/><br/>Why oh why are there so many freaking 5 Star reviews for this???? I can only think that a lot of female readers get a whiff of what they are told is an Alpha Male and their brains cease to function correctly.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>ROME IS <i>NOT</i> AN ALPHA MALE. NOT ANYWHERE CLOSE</u>
</b><br/><br/>I actually liked the character of Rome up until about 25-30%, and later from about 75%.<br/><br/>The story is</span>
  <span id="freeText3174246805809220914" style="display:none"><b>My Review of SWEET HOME by Tilly Cole</b><br><br><b>1.5 stars, and that is for the beginning and the end. </b><br><br>Oops, I did it again – I fell for the hype, that is. <br><br>Why oh why are there so many freaking 5 Star reviews for this???? I can only think that a lot of female readers get a whiff of what they are told is an Alpha Male and their brains cease to function correctly.<br><br><b>
  <u>ROME IS <i>NOT</i> AN ALPHA MALE. NOT ANYWHERE CLOSE</u>
</b><br><br>I actually liked the character of Rome up until about 25-30%, and later from about 75%.<br><br>The story is about English 20 year old Molly Shakespeare from the North of England and Romeo Prince from Alabama, in America’s South.<br><br>Molly goes to Alabama to the college where Rome Prince is the star quarterback of the college football team. <i>Whatever.</i><br><br>Molly annoys the hell out of me from the beginning, when she first meets the male MC. He introduces himself as <b>
  <i>Rome.</i>
</b> Later, she finds out his name is actually Romeo, but he tells her that he doesn’t like Romeo, (he has good reason, we later find out why, it’s to do with his crappy parents) yet Molly CONTINUALLY calls him and refers to him as ROMEO??? WHY???<br><br>I can only think that the Author wanted to continually remind us of the Romeo and Juliette connection she was trying so hard to push, and thought that we might otherwise forget if he was referred to as Rome. *Massive eye roll*<br><br>There are so many things wrong with this story, for example, the accents??? Everyone (except Molly of course) speaks in exactly the same way that I am supposed to believe is a Southern drawl, dropping the ‘g’ of every word ending in ‘ing’ and other examples that really got on my nerves SO much after about 20%. However, our Molly, who don’t forget is from the North of England, appears to have no accent at all.<br><br><b>OH COME ON!!!</b> You can’t do an accent for every one else and not the other MC!!! Or are we supposed to believe that Molly speaks in that fake British posh accent that is overused in every American sitcom/teen drama/kids programme (with the exception of Frasier and the character of Daphne Moon – which is actually similar to how Molly would have sounded) <br><br>Given that a) She was bought up in the North of England and b) She was in the care system, foster care etc, there is no freaking way she would speak with anything other than a strong Northern twang, but not a mention of this.<br><br>I personally think it is better to stay away from attempting to write accents, preferring the Author to say (they all spoke with a deep Southern twang) and maybe give one example, then I can put the rest together in my head.<br><br>Apart from that, the characters all lacked any real depth. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>Show, don’t tell</u>
  </i>
</b><br><br>The Author seemed to forget this rule completely. During or after a scene, Molly would TELL you that Rome was angry/moody/aggressive/possessive etc but when I read the scene back, I just didn’t get it??? And when you did realise he was any of these things, it didn’t make sense then either because it would come out of the blue with no reason????<br><br>It would appear the Author was trying too hard to make Rome an Alpha Male, and a young (wannabe) Dominant. Instead, he just came across as a spoilt little dipshit, which in itself made absolutely no sense at all because he definitely wasn’t a spoilt child, if anything he was neglected/abused.<br><br>The character representation of the side characters didn’t fair any better, with Rome’s parents coming across as though they were starring in an evil parody!! Seriously, I nominate Cruella DeVille for Rome’s ridiculous mother!!<br><br><b>
  <i>“Rome faced his parents. “You’re the worst fuckin’ people I’ve ever known. I’m your only son and you cant stand me, have ever even loved me? Ever just once felt anything for me?”<br>Mr and Mrs prince looked at each other and cracked up, their cackles echoing around the grand room. I was convinced I’d just witnessed the personification of pure evil.</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=kd0ajb" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389189363ra/8002522.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>That’s just one example. There are many more, but I cant be bothered to go into detail. The scenes between Molly and Mrs Prince later in the book are farcical. <br><br>The sex scenes. Get a bucket ready. For a start, Molly lets Rome have sex with her without a condom, <i>because she’s on the pill</i> Did no-one tell these two about STI’s??? Good God. This, I have noticed, is a growing trend in NA/YA novels. <br><br><i>
  <u>
    <b>Listen up, and listen good – PROTECT YOURSELVES,!! Don’t take any chances with your health, if he or neither of you want to use a condom, insist you both get tested first. It’s only fair and the correct thing to do to keep both of you safe.</b>
  </u>
</i> *Preaching over*<br><br>It has been said that these scenes are what might possibly be the reasons for the 5 Stars, but I can’t see why. Molly is relatively inexperienced – just one sexual experience that was apparently not much of one (yawn) whilst of course Rome is the stereotypical man whore who has shed loads of experience. <br><br>All he does is treat her badly in the sex scenes, roughly, making her say particular things as he takes her “rough and hard”. He hardly ever makes love to her, treats her gently, or shows her affection during sex,<br><br><b>
  <i>“He fucks me like he hates me. . .”</i>
</b><br><br>Yea, real romantic that, such a sweetheart. A real keeper, this one. And. . .<br><br><b>
  <i>"Romeo regained his lust laden expression and leaned in towards me, “We’re goin’ to the cabin. I’m gonna strip you down and you’re gonna do everythin’ I say, until neither of us cant stand. You get me?”</i>
</b><br><br>Well, not too bad, except that at this point Molly <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ is in the early stages of pregnancy. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Again, I think this was the Author trying to inject the D/s element into the story. Whatever. <br><br>Rome does redeem himself towards the last 20%, and the ending is actually really quite good. It has one of the best dialogues Ive read in a long time, just before his big football game, <br><br><b>
  <i>“Hey, Mol.”<br>“Hey, you”<br>“You gonna give up that sweet kiss?”<br>“If that’s what you want”<br>“It most definitely fuckin is”</i>
</b><br><br>Okay, maybe you have to be there, in the moment, but it is lovely. <br><br>All in all though I was very disappointed with this one. I got really bored by 50% and almost DNF.<br><br><b>Will I ever find my Alpha Male worthy of multi stars?? My search continues . . . .</b><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12079110861619192133"><i>
  <b>The amount of total L-O-V-E I have for this book is just crazy.... This one just hit all my spots in all the right places at just the right time.. You know how it is.. sometimes you're in the mood for some sweet NA with some good steam and when you get your hands on the perfect one it's like...</b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383185007ra/6431351.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Well yep, that was Sweet Home.. Not only do we get the uber sexy sin on a stick quarterback Romeo, aka Rome, we also get some good ole SEC Football ( Roll Tide), a quirky braineack that doesnt know her</span>
  <span id="freeText12079110861619192133" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>The amount of total L-O-V-E I have for this book is just crazy.... This one just hit all my spots in all the right places at just the right time.. You know how it is.. sometimes you're in the mood for some sweet NA with some good steam and when you get your hands on the perfect one it's like...</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383185007ra/6431351.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Well yep, that was Sweet Home.. Not only do we get the uber sexy sin on a stick quarterback Romeo, aka Rome, we also get some good ole SEC Football ( Roll Tide), a quirky braineack that doesnt know her own sex appeal, a college campus setting, and a heart warming True LOVE story.. <br><br>First let's feast our eyes on AMAZEBALLS Romeo Prince.. Starting QB for the Alabama Crimson Tide ( Roll Tide) ( side note.. if you live in the deep south.. pointing to self, and LOVE SEC football..still pointing to self.. Roll Tide just comes out whenever you talk Bama football. Thats just the way it is. Roll Tide) ANYWAYSSSSSS.... Romeo.. yep, so so sooooo sexy. Godlike on the football field. Senior. Destined for greatness in the NFL. Chicks love him and he has no short supply of all types of hoochie mama's wanting to drop their panties for Rome. He's seriously got it going on HARD. <br><br>Rome...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383185007i/6431352._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then we've got sweet Molly.. so cute and soooo smart! She's also sexy but she hides it well behind her sexy librarian glasses and hair buns. She's from England but traveled all the way to Alabama to assist her philosophy professor for one year. She's got some really cool roomies though that are determined to break her out of her shell and show her what college life is all about... parties, sororities, gettin naked, and generally how to have a blast. <br><br>Molly...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383185777i/6431550._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Rome and Mol crash into each other in the hall on the way to class and of course it's insta chemistry.. Molly is a little tongue tied and Rome is ALOT interested. What intrests him the most though.. is that this beautiful girl doesn't seem to have a freaking clue who he is. He's used to girls fawning all over him.. especially one skank ho bitch that seriously will NOT leave him alone ( I want to cut this bitch). But Molly wants to avoid him if at all possible. He give her all kinds of tingles and she's not looking for tingles.... See, Molly's got some serious heartache inside. She's lived a tough life and has experienced some great sadness in her life. She doesn't open up to anyone and she likes it that way. Then Rome.. Rome may seem to have it all on the outside but his family life is total shit. He's got some of the shitiest parents totally everrrrr. Like ever and ever. They really suck. Total suck monkey ass suck. Yes. They suck. <br><br>ANYWAY.. What when Rome decides that someone like Molly is just what he needs, he goes after her. Sweet Mol really never stood a chance. But Rome shows her a side that no one else sees. For some reason he feels like he can really open up to her and Molly feels the same. They have a connection.. a once in a lifetime connection...<br><br><br>But the road isn't easy for them...With a vendictive wanna be girlfriend, evil parents, and tragedy along the way.. things get rough. Really rough.... But this is a love so strong ...built from the ground up. <br>Yep, we get a seriously amazing story and a sweet HEA... but it's the journey for them that will pull you in. I was so wrapped up in Romeo and Molly that I hated for their story to end. So so good. <br><br>Don't let this one pass you up!! <br><br><br></span>

<div id="review_743075435" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/743075435" />
    <a title="K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16359109-k"><img alt="K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357989852p2/16359109.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/743075435?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K" href="/user/show/16359109-k">K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=angsty">angsty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=tattooed-pierced-hero">tattooed-pierced-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=arrogant-hero">arrogant-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=hero-alpha-obsessed-jealous">hero-alpha-obsessed-jealous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=messed-up-hero">messed-up-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=love-the-heroine">love-the-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=messed-up-heroine">messed-up-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16359109-k?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer743075435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3607069730946149368"><b>5 'Romeo O' Romeo' Stars!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384037133i/6753133.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>It only took Romeo one look at Juliet and his fate was sealed. Maybe I’m just like my namesake, and maybe you’re just like yours.</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This book was an unexpected surprise! I was seeing this book on everyone's reading list and figured I'd give it a shot. I love when I immerse myself in a book that I don't have high expectations for and then end up falling in love with it! That's what <i>Sweet Home</i> was for me...a book that I fell absolutely in love with.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"One day, my sw</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText3607069730946149368" style="display:none"><b>5 'Romeo O' Romeo' Stars!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384037133i/6753133.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>It only took Romeo one look at Juliet and his fate was sealed. Maybe I’m just like my namesake, and maybe you’re just like yours.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>This book was an unexpected surprise! I was seeing this book on everyone's reading list and figured I'd give it a shot. I love when I immerse myself in a book that I don't have high expectations for and then end up falling in love with it! That's what <i>Sweet Home</i> was for me...a book that I fell absolutely in love with.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"One day, my sweet girl, some lucky man will come and help you understand the very meaning of love. He will sweep you off your feet and show you what it is to place your heart in someone else’s care, and to willingly offer them the gift of your soul."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Romeo and Molly. Romeo and Juliet. Both names of people that have a tragically beautiful love. Both tell the story of forces trying to consume their love. A love that was meant to be. A love that is beyond anything either could have ever hoped for. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I don’t remember Romeo being this pushy with Juliet!”.....He arched his eyebrows meaningfully. “And look at how that worked out for them. My way is better—less death, more orgasms.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Romeo Prince</b> is the most desirable guy on campus. A guy that never commits to anyone. A guy that other guys are shit scared of and girls would gladly give a lung for. He has a broad chest, a deep southern drawl, long, dirty-blond hair, and is the quarterback for the Alabama Tides. <b>Molly Shakespeare</b> on the other hand is an English, painfully private introvert who has followed her professor to Alabama to be a teaching assistant. Both Romeo and Molly are in the wrong place at the right time when their worlds collide.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Why does any human want anyone? My body recognizes you as something that’s good for me. My mind recognizes you as someone who’s right for me, and my soul recognizes you as someone who is meant for me."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384042480i/6754406.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Romeo and Molly soon begin a relationship that they are trying to keep secret from everyone. They both have troubled pasts and ghosts that would destroy their love if they let them. They are trying to keep it a secret from Romeo's abusive parents and Molly just doesn't want to be seen as another one of Romeo Prince's latest conquests. Unfortunately, secrets have a funny way of coming out and sometimes, no matter how hard they might try to prevent it, their love is destined to be filled with heartbreak. <br><br>Romeo..sigh! I loved Romeo Prince. He is everything that I love in a hero. He is hot, protective, possessive and just the total alpha male package. Yes, he can be secretive. Yes, he's bossy and dominating. But he's also damaged and vulnerable. I just absolutely adored him. Molly was an awesome heroine. She was the lovable nerd that has suffered immense grief in her past that we can all relate to. Fantastic set of characters! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384042480i/6754407.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Romeo and Molly first meet they form an instant attraction. Romeo's long believed dead heart feels a pulse that he hasn't felt in years and Molly sees in Romeo the love that she's afraid to feel. Some people may think their relationship happens pretty fast, but I didn't feel that way. I loved the progression of their relationship, and swooned a good 50 percent of the novel.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384042480i/6754408.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There is so much more to this story than what I've said, but telling too much would be giving away spoilers that make this book so fantastic. This book isn't all roses and flowers. There is a good amount of sadness thrown in as well. LOVED IT! I have so many quotes for this book, I'm going to have to list some extras that I loved!<br><br><u>
  <b>My Favorite Quotes:</b>
</u><br><br><i>"We would love each other more than anyone in the history of the world ever had."<br><br>"Romeo Prince was a human kaleidoscope. He fucked me like he hated me, but his adoration and love was never too far from the surface—and I couldn’t imagine him in any other way."<br><br>“Just so you know. I’m gonna take you again tonight. Addicted, Shakespeare. I’m fuckin’ addicted.”<br><br>"I sobbed out a cry and bit the nail of my thumb to hold back the screams. “Yes, I’m yours.”<br>Rome pulled my thumb into his hand. “You’re gonna make me crazy with that move, Mol. I’d rather put an object more satisfying there if you need somethin’ to play with.”<br><br>“I get so lonely that at times, I literally think it might kill me.”<br>Romeo licked his bottom lip anxiously and his eyes began to glisten. “Can I tell you somethin’?” I nodded shyly. He ran his finger down my cheek, but almost as if the action fuelled his strength rather than gave me comfort. “I’m desperately lonely, too.”<br><br>“Fateful star-crossed lovers?” He smiled again. It was almost a full smile I’d never seen from him before, so careless and free. “I think we need to stop quotin’ that damn play, Shakespeare. I feel like we’re the fucked-up rated-R version of Romeo and Juliet.”</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1384043634i/6754601.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The writing was amazing. The characters were well rounded, dagamed, and lovable. The story itself was romantic, passionate, and swoon-worthy! I loved this book and even though some of the topics have been used before, I fell in love with the story nonetheless.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"A home is not a place. It’s not a country or a town or a building or possession. Home is with the other half of your soul, the person who shares in your grief and helps you carry the burden of loss. Home is with the person who throughout it all never gives up on you and brings you eternal happiness."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="3607069730946149368" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1242368476" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1242368476" />
    <a title="AJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3143126-aj"><img alt="AJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406382884p2/3143126.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1242368476?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AJ" href="/user/show/3143126-aj">AJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=omg-romantic">omg-romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=sports-star">sports-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=series-book-1">series-book-1</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=pb-i-own">pb-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=series-faves-book-1">series-faves-book-1</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1242368476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13699030713681702956"><b>OMGOMGOMG!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382462243ra/5902047.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>5 huge stars.</b><br/><br/>Why the hell did it take me so long to read this book? Gorgeous, manwhoring quarterback and an intelligent ‘good girl’, both slightly broken, but absolutely perfect for each other - it’s a story that’s been done before, but THIS book truly shines in a sea of NA books that have a similar set up. The writing is wonderful, the characters are amazing, and there is an engaging and heart-pounding love story that is funny, sweet, sexy and emotional with none of the pointless dram</span>
  <span id="freeText13699030713681702956" style="display:none"><b>OMGOMGOMG!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382462243ra/5902047.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>5 huge stars.</b><br><br>Why the hell did it take me so long to read this book? Gorgeous, manwhoring quarterback and an intelligent ‘good girl’, both slightly broken, but absolutely perfect for each other - it’s a story that’s been done before, but THIS book truly shines in a sea of NA books that have a similar set up. The writing is wonderful, the characters are amazing, and there is an engaging and heart-pounding love story that is funny, sweet, sexy and emotional with none of the pointless drama or annoying behaviour that you often find in college-based books. I had that tingly feeling (you know, the one that you get when you're reading something special) from start to finish, and I thought it was absolutely fantastic!<br><br>Molly Shakespeare has moved from England to Alabama as part of her college studies. She has had a hard life but has worked hard to get where she is and she is determined to achieve her dreams of a PhD and a career as a College professor. She is experiencing a whole new world in the US, and her acclimatisation to all things college is a great addition to the story. Romeo ‘Rome’ Prince is the superstar of college football and headed straight for the NFL. He seems to have it all, but as perfect as his life may appear on the surface, there is so much more to him than what he shows. <br><br>From the moment they see each other, the chemistry is apparent and their initial encounters are brimming with sexual tension. Of course, Molly has no idea of who he is or why he is such a big deal, and in a world where he is the constant target of groupies, Rome likes that, but while he is smitten from the very beginning, Molly is hesitant to get involved with the campus playboy. But he is determined to have her, and as the perfect combination of sweet, playful and sexy as all hell, there’s no way Molly can resist him. <br><br><blockquote>
<i>“Don’t mistake yourself for one of the others, Mol. You’re much, much more. I’ll gladly convince anyone who thinks otherwise.” <br>“Why am </i>I<i> more? I don’t get it.”<br>“You just are. You somehow give me peace in my completely fucked-up world. You get me; no one has before. It’s that simple.”</i>
</blockquote><br>I love this relationship! They are truly gorgeous together - honest with each other and there is no game playing and the intensity that is between them develops into a soul-deep love that they both embrace whole-heartedly. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>“My body recognises you as something that’s good for me. My mind recognises you as someone who’s right for me, and my soul recognises you as someone who is meant for me.” <br>A bashful smile ghosted his lips and his tense shoulders relaxed. “We’re in fuckin’ deep, aren’t we, Shakespeare?” he said in hushed tone, his body radiating a peaceful happiness. <br>A feeling of contentment settled over us both. <br>“I think that’s an understatement.”</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br>Is there anything sexier than a guy in complete, open, proud and unapologetic love? Add in the fact that he used to be a moody, manwhoring bastard, and it’s like romance reader crack, and I lapped up every moment of it.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I love you. I love you beyond anythin’ I could’ve ever imagine was possible.”</i>
</blockquote><br>The swoony declarations are balanced perfectly with the rawness of their relationship. They are completely open to each other, and that translates into some seriously intense sexy time! Rome likes control in the bedroom, and he demonstrates that over and over again, and oh holy hell, it’s hot! And rounding out the sweet and sexy, and the intensity between Rome and Molly, there are lots of light moments which had me laughing out loud. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I don’t remember Romeo being this pushy with Juliet!” <br>He arched his eyebrows meaningfully. “And look at how that worked out for them. My way is better— less death, more orgasms.”</i>
</blockquote><br>But Rome is dealing with cruel and overbearing parents who have their own plans for his life, and Molly’s past continues to plague her. They may have each other, but they have a lot that they have to overcome in order to get their happy ending, and OMG, the feels! My heart broke for them both as the story played out, and though I read with tears streaming down my face at times, I really like the way the conflict was written into the story <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[though I think Rome’s parents seemed a bit over-vilified. Are there really people like this out there? And if so, why hadn’t he ditched them long ago? But whatever, it added drama and didn’t diminish my love for the story at all <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I love the strength of their relationship through it all, and I thought that it was really well handled – minimally angsty yet incredibly emotional, and it’s all worth it for the incredible ending that had my heart pounding while I clutched my kindle with glee.<br><br><blockquote>
<i>“We can’t erase the secrets and marred memories of our pasts, but we can build the next chapter of our lives </i>together.”</blockquote><br>The Shakespeare theme is incorporated in a way that is playful, yet sweet, and there is a great group of characters that add a lot to the story, and have me excited to carry on with the series. <br><br>I honestly loved EVERYTHING about this book. I am in so much love with it that I’m going straight on to Sweet Rome, which is essentially the same story told from Rome’s POV. I can’t get enough, and I’m eager to experience it all over again.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Hey Mol.”<br>“Hey You.”<br>“You gonna give up that lucky sweet kiss?”<br>“If that's what you want.”<br>“It most definitely is.”</i>
</blockquote><br>I absolutely loved it, an instant favourite – 5 stars.<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="13699030713681702956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_744946624" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/744946624" />
    <a title="Amy | Foxy Blogs" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs"><img alt="Amy | Foxy Blogs" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366176904p2/9955253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/744946624?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy | Foxy Blogs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy | Foxy Blogs" href="/user/show/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs">Amy | Foxy Blogs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Amy | Foxy Blogs by: </span>
      Lisa Jayne, Anna, Kara
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs?shelf=october-2013">october-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs?shelf=2013-books-i-ve-read">2013-books-i-ve-read</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer744946624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3163126222562590363">**3.5 Star-Crossed stars**<br/><br/>A modern day Romeo & Juliet story that left me wavering between 3 and 4 stars...<br/><br/><b>Rome (Romeo) Price</b> is an all-star Alabama Crimson Tide star quarterback. His interfering and overbearing parents control his every move.<br/><br/><b>Molly <i>Juliet</i> Shakespeare</b> is a shy introverted brainiac. She has traveled from England to attend college in Alabama.<br/><br/>These two lonely hearts find each other. <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"The world deserves to have who think of others before themselves, that strive to be less self</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText3163126222562590363" style="display:none">**3.5 Star-Crossed stars**<br><br>A modern day Romeo &amp; Juliet story that left me wavering between 3 and 4 stars...<br><br><b>Rome (Romeo) Price</b> is an all-star Alabama Crimson Tide star quarterback. His interfering and overbearing parents control his every move.<br><br><b>Molly <i>Juliet</i> Shakespeare</b> is a shy introverted brainiac. She has traveled from England to attend college in Alabama.<br><br>These two lonely hearts find each other. <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"The world deserves to have who think of others before themselves, that strive to be less selfish and superficially concerned."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br>The power of Molly's pre-game kiss with Rome has all of fans considering her as Rome's good luck charm. <b>THE KISS SEEN AROUND THE STADIUM!</b><br><br>KA fans will like Rome because he is a college age alpha. <i>"You get me"?!</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382333130ra/5826135.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>SERIES:</b><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18105011.Sweet_Home__Sweet_Home___1_" title="Sweet Home (Sweet Home, #1) by Tillie Cole" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1376473414s/18105011.jpg" alt="Sweet Home (Sweet Home, #1) by Tillie Cole" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18759341.Sweet_Rome__Sweet_Home___2_" title="Sweet Rome (Sweet Home, #2) by Tillie Cole" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://www.goodreads.com/assets/nocover/60x80.png" alt="Sweet Rome (Sweet Home, #2) by Tillie Cole" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18759345.Sweet_Fall__Sweet_Home___3_" title="Sweet Fall (Sweet Home, #3) by Tillie Cole" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://www.goodreads.com/assets/nocover/60x80.png" alt="Sweet Fall (Sweet Home, #3) by Tillie Cole" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18759355.Sweet_Hope__Sweet_Home___4_" title="Sweet Hope (Sweet Home, #4) by Tillie Cole" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://www.goodreads.com/assets/nocover/60x80.png" alt="Sweet Hope (Sweet Home, #4) by Tillie Cole" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>When the author wrote Sweet Home it was intended to be a <i>standalone</i> but because of the persistence of readers to make this into a series she has turned into a 4 part series. <br>Book 1- Molly's POV. Book 2- Rome's POV. Book 3- Austin and Lexi's story. Book 4- Ally's story. For more info <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/5180638-sweet-home-is-now-a-series" rel="nofollow noopener">click here.</a></span>

<div id="review_743262834" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/743262834" />
    <a title="Charlotte Bugler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20206805-charlotte-bugler"><img alt="Charlotte Bugler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379529315p2/20206805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/743262834?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte Bugler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte Bugler" href="/user/show/20206805-charlotte-bugler">Charlotte Bugler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20206805-charlotte-bugler?shelf=half-wit-heroine">half-wit-heroine</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer743262834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5001449065050796081"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/>And that's me being generous..<br/><br/>For the people who've rated it 5 stars.. You should be <b>
  <u>BANNED</u>
</b> from rating on good reads and your opinions are now invalid.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383668834ra/6628757.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The only reason it got such high ratings is because of the steamy scenes, which frankly, were nothing special.<br/>I think the main problem with this book is that they act like they know each other and are in love when they've only met, like, <b>TWICE! WTF!!!</b> I'll tell you now, that immediately got me worried that I wasted £1.99 on on an ins</span>
  <span id="freeText5001449065050796081" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br>And that's me being generous..<br><br>For the people who've rated it 5 stars.. You should be <b>
  <u>BANNED</u>
</b> from rating on good reads and your opinions are now invalid.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383668834ra/6628757.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The only reason it got such high ratings is because of the steamy scenes, which frankly, were nothing special.<br>I think the main problem with this book is that they act like they know each other and are in love when they've only met, like, <b>TWICE! WTF!!!</b> I'll tell you now, that immediately got me worried that I wasted £1.99 on on an insta-love romance that quite frankly wasn't believable at all. Don't get me wrong, I love a bit of love at first sight, I'm not a pessimist, but I expect them to have a build up of a relationship. NOT act like your already in a relationship when you've only said a few words to each other! *RANTING*<br><br>I'm not going to write a very long review on this book because there's not really that much to say to be honest.. I was thoroughly disappointed considering the ratings and reviews, and no I didn't big it up too much and that's why I'm let down. It really just was a book that seemed like it was written by a woman who was just writing her perfect love-fantasy-boyfriend which, yes, every girl wants, but it was just unbelievable.<br>I get that the book was trying to show how the couples damaged past was effecting their relationship and the consequence of how they are now and the whole dominating/submissive relationship but I just wish the girl wouldn't take his shit all the time. I get he's had a bad past and has anger problems, but seriously! He got angry over nothing and she ended up apologising for nothing!<br>E.g..<br>Their at a club and one of the girls he's slept with were serving them and making comments and ended with her saying that his girlfriend was a skank basically and that his standards have dropped. She gets shitty and walks off to have him follow and have a go at her! With her then calming down after and saying she overreacted and blah blah blah. <br>I mean SERIOUSLY?! Please tell me other girls aren't actually like this! It's embarrassing! I would like to think that the majority of us girls don't get so manipulated.. <br><br>Also, I found the parents WAY over the top. I get their the villains of this book.<br>But tone it down a notch! I just thought it was way over the top.. What they did just isn't even worth talking about. The scenarios were really that ridiculous.<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/Evil%20laugh" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/585391.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Apart from all that.. It was an easy read. If you want an unrealistic romance that overcomes evil and manages to overcome all the devastation, and hot guy who just so happens to be rich, (because that never happens) who falls for a geeky and unpopular girl (shocker), with some sexy scenes then I'd recommend this book for you.<br>If your like me and prefer your female characters to have some balls, then I'd put off reading this for when you want to have an easy read with a fairytale love.<br><br>And on my last note, I'm going to part with saying that her best mate cass should of been a bigger part of the book as she was just awesome and ballsy and her sex sounds much better!<br><br><b>(notice that I have not mentioned the two main characters names. I have just finished the book and I can't remember. Only the best friends! Something's wrong with that)</b></a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5001449065050796081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2120077240" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2120077240" />
    <a title="Dilek VT" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49572641-dilek-vt"><img alt="Dilek VT" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448923258p2/49572641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2120077240?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dilek VT" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dilek VT" href="/user/show/49572641-dilek-vt">Dilek VT</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49572641-dilek-vt?shelf=sports-novel">sports-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49572641-dilek-vt?shelf=emotional-but-not-hot">emotional-but-not-hot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49572641-dilek-vt?shelf=college-students">college-students</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120077240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17637262454693837564">That was a sweet and touching love story between two damaged souls. Life has taken a lot from them and these two lonely souls find salvation in each other. It was an OK read for me, good but not good enough.<br/><br/><b>“We held on to each other as if we were one another’s lifeline.”</b><br/><br/>They are college students. The hero also plays football and he is the star quarterback of Alabama. The heroine is British whereas the hero is American. <br/><br/>Their story is emotional and heart-warming but definitely not hot enough. The</span>
  <span id="freeText17637262454693837564" style="display:none">That was a sweet and touching love story between two damaged souls. Life has taken a lot from them and these two lonely souls find salvation in each other. It was an OK read for me, good but not good enough.<br /><br /><b>“We held on to each other as if we were one another’s lifeline.”</b><br /><br />They are college students. The hero also plays football and he is the star quarterback of Alabama. The heroine is British whereas the hero is American. <br /><br />Their story is emotional and heart-warming but definitely not hot enough. The mildly hot scenes didn’t appeal to me at all as I don’t like dom-sub relationship. Still, I understood why he needed control during sex, but that didn’t make me like it at all.<br /><br />There are inconsistencies in my opinion as to character development. I sometimes questioned what they did or didn't do.<br /><br />The heroine Molly Juliet Shakespeare has a very high IQ and has been very successful in her education so far but still she cannot use that IQ in matters of heart or relationship issues. That was weird. For example, if your boyfriend and his cousin tell you that his parents are evil and they are planning something bad for them when they invited them to dinner, you shouldn't be so naive and believe that showing them how happy you are together will change their mind. No need to be Pollyanna here, everything is so clear.<br /><br />The hero Romeo (aka Rome) Prince is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[an abused child <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and he is aggressive when someone pisses him off and he is control freak in sex. <br /><br />His mood changes were understandable but the way he speaks to Molly while talking about feelings suddenly changes when he wants sex and it was weird for me. I couldn't get used to the switch between emotional Rome, who begs her not to leave him and the controlling Rome, who tells her she can't do anything without asking permission. It sounded unreal and ridiculous to me. <br /><br />As you may have already realized, they have the names of star-crossed lovers and Rome climbs to her room all the time. Again... weird stuff for me and unnecessary?! <br /><br />The parents in the book are pure evil. I wish they were punished for what they did but I wasn’t happy with the result at all.<br /><br /><b>Writing:</b><br /><br />The book is written by 1st person point of view (by the heroine only). That was another thing I disliked. I needed to know what was in the hero’s mind most of the time. <br /><br />Now, Book 1,5 tells their love story from the hero’s point of view. I don’t feel like reading the same events now told by the hero. It could easily have been one book told by dual point of view, what is the purpose of writing it this way? Publishing 2 books, I guess…<br /><br />Well, I want to read the other books in the series so maybe I might have a quick &amp; fast reading of Book 1,5 and then maybe write a longer review afterwards. This is all I want to say about Book 1 now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17637262454693837564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1218354446" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1218354446?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❥ KAT ❥ Kitty Kats Crazy About Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❥ KAT ❥ Kitty Kats Crazy About Books" href="/user/show/6245313-kat-kitty-kats-crazy-about-books">❥ KAT ❥ Kitty Kats Crazy About Books</a>

<div id="review_1469912288" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1469912288" />
    <a title="Barbara➰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13710123-barbara"><img alt="Barbara➰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561821906p2/13710123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1469912288?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara➰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara➰" href="/user/show/13710123-barbara">Barbara➰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13710123-barbara?shelf=dirty-talker">dirty-talker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13710123-barbara?shelf=favorite-couples">favorite-couples</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13710123-barbara?shelf=loved-the-way-he-loved-her">loved-the-way-he-loved-her</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13710123-barbara?shelf=insta-love">insta-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13710123-barbara?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13710123-barbara?shelf=alpha">alpha</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13710123-barbara?shelf=read-multiple-times">read-multiple-times</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13710123-barbara?shelf=sports">sports</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13710123-barbara?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13710123-barbara?shelf=ott-hero">ott-hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1469912288" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3284263888342646879"><b>Reread August 2017</b><br/><br/>It's been almost 2 years since I read this. It's just as emotional, heartbreaking and beautiful as it was the first time. The drama was OTT but I absolutely love their relationship. And Romeo steals my heart every time. I know I will reread it again. <br/><br/><b>Originally read December 2015</b><br/><br/>***5 I-Get-You-Romeo stars<br/><br/>I have actually been thinking and thinking about how to review this book. Ultimately, I want a book that touches me and makes me feel something. This book did that in spades. I</span>
  <span id="freeText3284263888342646879" style="display:none"><b>Reread August 2017</b><br /><br />It's been almost 2 years since I read this. It's just as emotional, heartbreaking and beautiful as it was the first time. The drama was OTT but I absolutely love their relationship. And Romeo steals my heart every time. I know I will reread it again. <br /><br /><b>Originally read December 2015</b><br /><br />***5 I-Get-You-Romeo stars<br /><br />I have actually been thinking and thinking about how to review this book. Ultimately, I want a book that touches me and makes me feel something. This book did that in spades. I cried big, fat, ugly tears...my heart actually hurt. There were times I laughed (I loved the way Molly can give it right back to Romeo) and there were those awwww moments as well.<br /><br />Romeo (yes, his name is Romeo Prince) is a star quarter back for the University of Alabama Crimson Tide. Molly (middle name Juliet, last name Shakespeare...yep, that's her name) is from England studying to get her masters in philosophy and working as a teaching assistant at UA. They meet in the hall outside the lecture room where she will be assisting. Romeo is taken with her immediately as she is him.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>“I think we need to stop quotin’ that damn play, Shakespeare. I feel like we’re the fucked-up rated-R version of Romeo and Juliet.”</b>
</blockquote><br />Told entirely from Molly's POV, I never once felt Romeo was anything but devoted and totally in love with Molly. I don't usually like only one POV because you never get an idea of how the other person feels. This was not the case here. It was written in such a way that you could feel Romeo's emotions and his love for Molly.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>"You somehow give me peace in my completely fucked-up world. You get me; no one has before. It’s that simple.”</b>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <b>"My body recognises you as something that’s good for me. My mind recognises you as someone who’s right for me, and my soul recognises you as someone who is meant for me.”</b>
</blockquote><br />Romeo is treated horribly by his "parents" and I use that word loosely. They were FUCKING EVIL! I felt so bad for him and cried when he finally revealed his story. I wanted his parents to die a horrible death...maybe get hit by a train or something. They needed to be gone and let them live their lives. Molly has lost both her parents, and then her grandmother whom she lived with after. She has been alone for sometime.<br /><br />Romeo is very protective of Molly. He is dominant in the bedroom and some of his behavior could be construed as abusive by some readers. I never felt that way. I could always feel his love for her...and this was all told by her POV. He always stands up against others for her, even his parents and other students. He was fabulous. <br /><br />They both experience a horrible loss and again, I cried. It broke my heart. They heal eventually and get their HEA.<br /><br />Safety Gang: Major spoilers so do not read if you don't want to know<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br />Was Romeo a manwhore? Yes, but he never touches another girl after he meets Molly. He is all about her all the time. He says he wishes he had never been with any of those other girls. Usually, I don't like a manwhore but I'm okay as long as he is all about the h and in this case, he is.<br /><br />Was there OW drama? Yes, Molly does come face-to-face with some of the girls Romeo has been with. But, she is a brilliant girl and for the most part it doesn't bother her. There are a couple of times when she's confronted but she gives it right back and I was so proud of her. <br /><br />There is a girl, Shelly, who thinks she's going to marry Romeo. They are NEVER engaged. It's something his parents are trying to push on him but he doesn't want it. There are a couple of scenes where Molly sees him with Shelly and misunderstands the situation. What I loved was he quickly straightened it out. He made sure she knew it wasn't what it looked like and that she was it for him in every way.<br /><br />Molly's mom died in childbirth and her dad committed suicide when she was 6 I think.<br /><br />Romeo's parents are physically and verbally abusive to him. It is horrible. It broke my heart and I felt so bad for him.<br /><br />Romeo's mother and father are horrible to Molly. His mother is physically abusive to her as well.<br /><br />Molly gets pregnant. She is on the pill, they had decided not to use condoms. He always has in the past. His mother slaps her, then pushes Molly into a desk and it causes her to lose the baby. Again, I had big, ugly tears. Molly becomes depressed and can't deal with it all and leaves to go back to England. She comes back and they get their HEA.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I really want to read the next one, which is told from Romeo's POV, but right now, I'm not sure my emotions can take it. I also am looking forward to the other stories in this series but have a feeling they will be emotional as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3284263888342646879" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ULKDw2lgKpS3VkNTss7jPv/epywvxy9OMdscVRXRAPVS470U14a1iwgjyNZ6dxFtw1gELS2WMFqAcceIODSXBg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ddltSGeI/anXZzo3OtwfLbialZoJGA04HEKnDD+IRcZ3iFOf2W5itmgSsbLyZe1+hBw2mwtJEiyt6HzREm3SNQ==')})
  }

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10172853238789468134">Amazon & USA Today Best Selling Author, Tillie Cole, is a Northern girl through and through. She originates from a place called Teesside on that little but awesomely sunny (okay I exaggerate) Isle called Great Britain. She was brought up surrounded by her English rose mother -- a farmer's daughter, her crazy Scottish father, a savagely sarcastic sister and a multitude of rescue animals and horses.</span>
  <span id="freeText10172853238789468134" style="display:none">Amazon &amp; USA Today Best Selling Author, Tillie Cole, is a Northern girl through and through. She originates from a place called Teesside on that little but awesomely sunny (okay I exaggerate) Isle called Great Britain. She was brought up surrounded by her English rose mother -- a farmer's daughter, her crazy Scottish father, a savagely sarcastic sister and a multitude of rescue animals and horses. <br />Being a scary blend of Scottish and English, Tillie embraces both cultures; her English heritage through her love of HP sauce and freshly made Yorkshire Puddings, and her Scottish which is mostly demonstrated by her frighteningly foul-mouthed episodes of pure rage and her much loved dirty jokes.<br /><br />Having been born and raised as a Teesside Smoggie, Tillie, at age nineteen, moved forty miles north to the 'Toon', Newcastle-Upon-Tyne, where she attended Newcastle University and graduated with a Bachelor of Arts honours degree in Religious Studies. She returned two years later to complete a Post-Graduate Certificate in Teaching High School Social Studies. Tillie, regards Newcastle to be a home from home and enjoyed the Newcastle Geordie way of life for seven 'proper mint' and 'lush' years.<br /><br />One summers day, after finishing reading her thousandth book on her much loved and treasured Kindle, Tillie turned to her husband and declared, "D'you know, I have a great idea for a story. I could write a book." Several months later, after repeating the same tired line at the close of another completed story, she was scolded by her husband to shut up talking about writing a novel and "just bloody do it!" For the first time in eleven years, Tillie actually took his advice (he is still trying to get over the shock) and immediately set off on a crazy journey, delving deep into her fertile imagination. <br /><br />Tillie, ever since, has written from the heart. She combines her passion for anything camp and glittery with her love of humour and dark brooding men (most often muscled and tattooed – they’re her weakness!). She also has a serious side (believe it or not!) and loves to immerse herself in the complex study of World Religions, History and Cultural Studies and creates fantasy stories that enable her to thread serious issues and topics into her writing -- yep, there's more to this girl than profanity and sparkles!<br /><br />After six years of teaching high school Social Studies and following her Professional Rugby Player husband around Europe, they have finally given up their nomadic way of life and settled in Calgary, Alberta where Tillie spends most of her days (and many a late night) lost in a writing euphoria or pursuing a dazzling career as a barrel-racing, tasselled-chap wearing, Stetson-sporting cowgirl... Ye-haw!<br /></span>

Now hear the story from his lips: unbarred, uncensored, and raw to the bone.  It makes me laugh when I hear folks think Molly and I rushed into things too fast, spouting that we couldn\'t possibly have felt what we did for each other in such a short space of time. I say, how the hell would they know? We made it, didn\'t we? She became my whole life, didn\'t she? And as for my folks not being real, being true? Tell that to me aged ten, eleven, twelve—damn, all my bastard life—when I was never enough, when I was beaten until I bled for being too good at football and not being everything they\'d dreamed: the perfectly dutiful son. Tell that to thousands of kids around the world getting wailed on by asshole parents for whatever stupid reason; tell them evil don\'t exist in their eyes.  Fuck Romeo and Juliet. This is the story of me and my girl, from my lips. No mushy sentiment, no cheese, just the plain, hard truth, and, because I\'m feeling generous, I\'m going to let you in on more of our story too.  Sweet Rome is a New Adult Companion Novel to Sweet Home—contains adult content, sexual situations, and mature topics. He isn’t dark in looks or intimidating to everyone he meets. In fact, he’s quite the opposite. Haunted by a crippling shyness and the tragic events of his past, Levi spends his days with his head buried in his books or training hard for his college football team. Too timid to talk to girls, Levi stays as far away as possible and completely on his own… until he saves the life of a troubled pretty blonde, a troubled pretty blonde that might just be the exception to his rule.\n\nElsie Hall is homeless. Or at least that’s all anyone ever sees. Every day is a fight for survival on the cold streets of Seattle, every day a struggle to find food and keep warm. Alone in life—a life that’s dangerous and cruel—her will to keep going is an ever-losing battle. In her world of silence, Elsie has given up hope that her life will contain anything but constant struggle and pain… until the beautiful boy she has severely wronged comes to her rescue at precisely This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
